The last NPC census figure of 2006 reported a population of 9,013,534 for Lagos State, however this figure was used to project the 2020 population of the State based on the 2.6% national (Nigeria) growth rate (World Bank, 2019) as shown above. The result of the 2020 population projection gave a figure of 12,910,948 for Lagos State (UTNL; 2020). This project population figure (12,910,000) which was based on the 2006 NPC figure no doubt is a far cry from the current population of the State, thus further validating the earlier position of the Lagos State Government on the NPC figure as not being true representation of the State's population.

Thus, the location, investments in infrastructural development by the successive governments of Lagos State as well as the socio-economic opportunities has attracted continuous migration not only from other parts of Nigeria but across the globe especially from the West African-sub region thereby culminating into population surge with its potential to trigger urban slum, overstretch infrastructures and more importantly natural resource depletion. It is important to mention that the attained urban trend coupled with uncontrolled population surge in the State remains a topical challenge confronting the State.

This has resulted in the astronomical population growth of the State and hence, the most densely populated in Nigeria with an estimated population of over 15 million people in 2013 and a projected population of 22 million in 2019.

As earlier stated, structured questionnaire were administered to stakeholders in the study area in order to obtain necessary socio-economic information of the project area. The returned questionnaires together with the perspectives or views of the strata of respondents on the project were consequently analyzed.

**Landownership/Acquisition**

Land tenure and management of water resources and access to basic resources in the project area seem to be in the control of the main native of the community and the government. Both government and private individual have been acquiring lands in the community to serve different purposes on the larger Lagos State community, and beyond. Land resources which used to be available for farming activities before urbanization have ceased as the entire project area has now become home of expensive property.

**4.14 Demography characteristics of sampled respondents**

This section of the report describes the demographic characteristics of the sampled respondents. As previously said a structured questionnaire were administered to a total of fifty (50) respondents in the study area while a total of 45 were returned and processed for analysis. The respondents were selected through stratified random sampling technique. The returned questionnaires together with the perspectives or views of the strata of respondents on the project were consequently analyzed. Data presented in this section was drawn from the survey.

**Age Distribution of Respondents**

The gender distribution of the respondents as contained in Table 4.38 shows that respondents in the age group category constitute 38.7% while those above 40 years constitute 34.6%. The low distribution recorded for youths (less than 19 years) could be adduced to their engagement in school and other vocations. The male constitute 66% while female is 34% and the high number of male respondents can be attributed to the dominance nature of men in the society as most of them engage in various occupation (NURTW, motorcycle-Okada/tricycle riding) while women were majorly petty traders with their shops / kiosks by the roadside or under the near-by bridge.

The marital status of the respondents as depicted in Table 4.39 shows that nearly all the respondents are married and this was expected considering the age and distribution earlier reported. All the marriages are monogamous with most of the respondents reported having not more than three children in their families as expected of the nature of people living in the project area. **Description of sample respondents by Religion, Customs, Beliefs Systems and Cultural Heritage**

The religion affiliation of the respondents in the study area shows that we have Christians, Muslims and traditional worshippers alike. However, Christianity and Islam are the two major religions being practiced by the residents in the sampled community. As indicated 54.9% and 42.7% were Christian and Muslims respectively while a fraction of 2.4% of the community claimed to engaged in traditional religious practices.

**Description of Sample Respondents by Ethnic Composition**

The surveyed community is heterogeneous in ethnic composition. The sampled respondents is made up of Yoruba ethnic groups of different dialectic groups from different part of southwestern Nigeria. The native of the community are mostly Yoruba speaking people. However, it is appreciated that the community equally have other ethnic groups which include Igbo, Hausa, Ijaw amongst others. Majority of the sampled respondents are Ijebu and Awori speaking people representing 59.7% of the ethnic composition while 41.3% is of other ethnic extraction.

**Description of Sample Respondents by Educational Characteristics**

Considering the educational attainment of the inhabitants, statistics shows that the sampled residents in the study area have attended primary school and secondary schools with few of them also noticed to have passed a tertiary education. Although Lagos State is one of the states with high literacy level, the data from the household survey shows that this align with the level of education in Lagos. This data displayed in Table 4.40 shows that women, particularly street traders have lower literacy levels than men. This aligns with the information during the FGDs and KIIs that more girls drop out of school at an early age. The lower education attainment of people within the project area, particularly women may result in many local people being able to take up employment opportunities with the project. This will be considered in planning for employment to ensure local communities within the project area receives support to ensure that more local people can take advantage of project related employment opportunities.

**Description of income Distribution of Sampled Residents**

Statistics from the survey revealed that the sampled respondents are engaged in both formal and informal income generating activities. Some of the respondents have employment or business enterprises within and around their abode. Other have their income generating activities far from their residence. According to the findings, the sampled respondents are engaged in occupation such as trading/marketing, transport, fishing, crafts/artisan, service/other wage jobs. It is interesting to note also that some of the inhabitants of the community are retirees. The result of the distribution of respondents by monthly income earnings revealed rural/or peri-urban nature of the study area where more than half of the respondents earns less than N40,000.00 unlike what is obtainable in the cosmopolitan area where majority can earn more than N40,000.00 a month. Considering the income generated by the respondents in the study area vis a vis the current economic realities in the country, their income can be assumed to be relatively small.

**4.15 Existing Infrastructure and Facilities**

The level of infrastructures and amenities available and functional in any area or community has direct implications on the quality of life in that area, and therefore determines the willingness of people to live and remain there. It also influences other socio-cultural and economic variables in the area. A reasonable level of income, availability and access to basic infrastructural amenities of life has always been used as a measure of quality of life.

**Educational Facilities**

It is a known fact that no society can develop above the quality of its human capital. This recognition can be adduced to the high number of educational institutions in Lagos State. Ipakodo/Ebute-Iga communities are blessed with a number of public institutions. These include: Ipakodo Senior Grammar school, Ipakodo Junior Grammar school, Ipakodo primary school for physically challenged children, Ipakodo Junior High school, Ipakodo Senior High school.

**Power Supply**

The project host community is well connected to electricity supply from the national grid through Ikeja Electricity Distribution (IEDC) facility with street light also conspicuously noticed along the main access road to the community. However, there are numerous residents utilizing generators to light their premises. Other sources of energy especially for cooking within the project area are Liquefied Petroleum Gas (LPG), firewood, charcoal.

**Transportation**

The means of transportation within the surveyed community are commercial tricycle, Motor cycles (otherwise referred to Okada), cab and medium light buses with the last two serving as major commuter transportation mode from the Lagos metropolitan to the community and vice versa. Many of the residents of the community do not own a car of their own but largely depend on the aforementioned transportation mode.

**Communication**

The project area is well served with communication network and facilities. This has a strong implication on the socio- economic development activities of the area. Mobile phone services like Globacom, Airtel, 9Mobile, MTN are present in the area. All these facilities will facilitate communication during the implementation and operational phase of the project.

**4.16 Community Health Environment and Related Issues**

**Water Supply**

Access to portable water is one of the Sustainable Development Goals and is measured by the percentage of the population with safe drinking water in their dwelling or located within a convenient distance from the user's dwelling (UN 1996). According to the United Nations, safe water includes treated surface waters and untreated but uncontaminated water such as that from protected boreholes, springs and sanitary wells. The community has no public water supply as most of the residents obtain water supply from well and borehole systems dug within their premises.

Finding during the FGD revealed that water from these two facilities are not drinkable as most premises owner cannot afford the required expensive treatment process that can make the water safe for drinking. Water from these facilities are usually used for cooking, washing and other domestic related activities. The well water systems in most cases are located in an open spaces in front of the premises with an unrestricted access to the facility by neighbours. The residents claimed to rely on sachet water and other treated bottled like water for drinking purposes within the community.

**Health Care Facilities, Morbidity Patterns and Health Management:**

Health is a state of complete physical, mental and social wellbeing, without any form of infirmity. In examining development in the health domain, the main issues vital to the health of the citizenry include access of the people to social and health facilities, availability of health facilities, availability of health care services, survival chances and the issue of reproductive health. The measurement of access to health care services is based on the number of health facilities per 1000 people. In other words, accessibility to health care services is conceptualized on the number of health and service centers (primary, secondary and tertiary) available per 1000 people. The life expectancy estimates for Lagos State is the same as the national estimate.

The world Health Organization (W.H.O) in its World Health Statistics 2006 estimated that life expectancy for men in Nigeria are 42 years and 47 years for women. Critically, fertility of the populace is important and is best measured by the Total Fertility Rate (TFR), which is an indication of the total number of children a woman is estimated to have in her productive lifetime. Existence of precise estimates of the TFR values for this L.G.A could not be ascertained as no values were available, however, the National Bureau of Statistics estimates the value for the South-West Geo Political Zone as 4.6 while the national average is 5.25 children born / woman. (Annual Abstract of Statistics, 2013).

**Table 4.41: Under 5 Mortality and Maternal Mortality Ratio (MMR) per 100,000 in the various geo-political zones of Nigeria**
| Geo-political Zones | Number Under 5 Mortality per 1000 | Number of Maternal Mortality Ratio (MMR) per 100,000 |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| North-west Zone | 269 Children | 1549 Women |
| North-East Zone | 260 Children | 1026 Women |
| South-West Zone | 176 Children | 286 Women |
| South-East Zone | 103 Children | 165 Women |
*Source: UNICEF Child Malnutrition and Mortality in Nigeria, Report 2013*

The community has no presence of public hospital. The available private medical center in the area is relatively expensive for the residents. Therefore, most residents who desire to seek medical assistance usually attend Badagry General Hospital which is located at an estimated 4.5km away from the community for treatment.

**Basic Sanitation / Waste Management**

According to the WHO, sanitation is defined as facilities and services for the safe disposal of human urine and faeces. The synergy between water and sanitation stems from the fact that both work together to reduce the pathogen load in the ambient environment, and in the interruption of the transmission of the pathogens. The accumulation of waste products and their indiscriminate disposal represent a grave hazard to health of the general populace. Systems of waste disposals are designed to eliminate these hazards. Access to basic sanitation is conceptualized on the proportion of the total population with access to sanitary facilities for human waste disposal in the dwelling or immediate vicinity. Ideally, there should be at least one latrine for each family, and the facility should always be kept clean. The environment is well maintained and attractive. Most parts of the estate are well landscaped and there are green areas in front of houses.

Most homes within the study area have good toilet facilities. Personal water closet was the commonest method (99.9%) for sewage disposal in the households. Generally, observation show that refuse disposal practices is fair. Waste management in the study area is handled by private waste management concessioner approved by the Lagos state Waste Management Authority. According to the study by Obianuju B, et al (2018), Lagos produces 13 million Kg of solid wastes every day without adequate solid waste handling facilities.

**Housing In the Project Area**

The provision of good housing is an important aspect of environmental health as it represents a significant part of man's environment. The project area is rural community with most houses still representing houses expected to see in rural areas. The houses within the project are of low quality structures that can be compared with some structural designs in a typical rural community across the Lagos State.

**Diseases Prevalence and Pattern**

Nigeria reportedly has high rates of infectious diseases, including HIV, malaria, Yellow fever, rabies, Hepatitis and Meningitis (CIA Fact-book 2010). According to the World Bank, in 2009, 4% percent of the population (aged 15-49) were infected with HIV, with higher rates of infection for women (3%) than for men (1%) (World Bank, 2010). Maternal mortality was estimated in 2008 to be 545 deaths per 100,000 live births (World Bank, 2010).

The W.H.O reports that in 2004, there were 5.0 deaths hospital beds per 10,000 people (W.H.O 2011). Nigeria's crude birth rate in 2009 was 40 per 1,000 people. The total fertility rate in 2009 was 6 births per woman (World Bank, 2010). Majority of the participants in the study area expressed a view that the general health status in the area is typical of that in Lagos State, which in turn is similar to the rest of Nigeria. Common illnesses mentioned included rheumatism, arthritis, malaria fever, typhoid, cough, skin conditions, diarrhea, pneumonia and respiratory tract infections.

The Focused Group Discussions (FGDs) conducted revealed that there was no incidence of HIV and Aids within the locality; however, it is recognized that this may be inaccurate owing to the social stigma associated with HIV/AIDS syndrome in many parts of the world especially Africa. With respect to STD like HIV, sexual risks behaviours such as multiple sexual partnerships, causal and unprotected sexual relationship, patronage of prostitutes as well as the use of illicit drugs and alcohol could be responsible. Table 4.42 shows the common diseases and their causes within the study area.

**Table 4.42: Common diseases within the study Area**
| Diseases | Predisposing Factors |
| :--- | :--- |
| Malaria | Bushes that provide mosquitoes breeding grounds. Stagnant water that provide breeding grounds for mosquitoes |
| Typhoid | Fecal contamination of source of drinking water. Poor Sanitary Conditions that contribute to fecal contamination. |
| Skin Conditions | Poor sanitation and personal hygiene practices that contribute to the spread of infection. |
| Diarrhea | Poor sanitation and personal hygiene practices that contribute to contamination |
| Pneumonia | Poor sanitation and personal hygiene practices that contribute to the spread of infection. Inadequate clothing and poor housing that contribute to incubation. |
| Respiratory Tract Infection | Over-crowding and poor sanitation. Indoor Air Pollution |
| Physical Deformities | Absence/Lack of Immunization. |

**4.17 Public Perception, Concerns of the Public about the Project**

The local community was keen to talk to the EIA field team on the proposed project and they were appreciative of the fact that the field team engaged them in Focus Group Discussion and also involved them in responding to the questionnaire in a consultative manner. The people encountered participated actively in raising their concerns and they expressed their hope that lawful procedures will be taken into consideration during the project implementation. The household respondents expressed various opinions about the proposed Container Terminal development project with more than half making favourable comments. The household respondents had more favourable opinions than the Key Informants. The reasons adduced by those in support of the project includes the following:
i. The proposed project will lead to further development of the community and the project area
ii. The proposed project will create employment opportunities and improvement in the socio-economic life of the people of the community.
iii. The project will boost businesses and reduce social vises as some idled hands will be employed especially during the site clearing and construction phase

However, one-fifth of the respondents had negative opinion about the project. These categories of respondents expressed dissenting views about the project as follows:
*   The project may encourage traffic bottleneck around the project area particularly along the Lagos-Badagry Expressway due to movement of cars and trucks supply goods from the Badagry Deep sea port in/out of the estate premises;
*   The project construction phase may increase STD infection in the project area due to influx of people seeking to patronize the company handling the construction work
*   The project may contribute to excessive consumption of resources such as energy, water and thus contributing to emission of greenhouse gases to the project area.
*   The project may lead to increase in rent and general prices of commodities and services. Although, this is debatable whether this is generally positive or negative. For instance, the landlords would probably be happy with increase in rent while tenants will be unhappy about the same
*   The project could lead to increase in air-borne diseases arising from the construction works
*   Increased in noise impact due to the use of construction machinery and equipment
*   Owners of some make shift shops located on the setback of Lagos-Badagry Highway in front of the proposed project site also expressed concerns that the project development will lead to demolition of their shops and that the proponent may count them worthy of compensation of loss of their means of livelihood

However, the stakeholders proposed some measures to mitigate their concerns on the project and this includes the following:
*   The proponent should show sincerity of purpose, openness, dialogue and carry all concerned stakeholders along in the course of implementing the project as this is expected to bring the foundation for a good proponent- community relationship.
*   Provision of employment and youth empowerment for people of the project area
*   Effective monitoring of waste reduction of environmental nuisances that may be created during the construction and residence/operation phase of the project.

### **CHAPTER FIVE: Potential and Associated Impacts**

**5.1 Introduction**

This chapter discusses the potential and associated impacts of the proposed project on the environmental, health and socio-economic characteristics of the project area. It equally presents an overview of the impact assessment methodology as well as results of impact screening and detailed qualitative and quantitative impact assessment. One of the primary intentions of every EIA study is to identify the associated and potential impacts of the proposed project and proffer measures to mitigate such impacts. The potential and associated impacts that would arise from the proposed project are identified and evaluated.

During construction for instance, most sites are particularly vulnerable to environmental disturbance. Construction is often a rapid and disorderly process, with strong emphasis on completing the project and not on protecting the environment (World Bank, 1991). This creates some impacts on the environment, which may be positive or negative. Some of the environmental changes, whether positive or negative would in some cases be irreversible. For instance, vegetation would be removed, exposing the soil to erosion and other disturbances, which in most case get exacerbated by excavation and grading. The assessment covers all aspects of the project from preconstruction, through construction and operations as well as decommissioning of the project. A key to successful Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA) is the use of appropriate impact identification and prediction methods. Generally, a number of impact assessment methods have been developed over the years and new approaches continue to emerge. All good methods have certain elements in common, which are widely accepted as essential to ElAs. Any good and widely acceptable impact assessment method (or technique) should address, at least, the following:

**Comprehensiveness**

The premise of a sound impact assessment is to ensure that any and all impact(s), no matter how remote their chances of occurring, are comprehensively assessed and discussed. Thus, a sound impact assessment method must, as a minimum, be capable of detecting the full range of important elements and combinations of elements. It must be innovative in considering possibilities, focusing not only on established possibilities typically associated with planned activities, but also directing attention to novel or unsuspected effects or impacts.

**Selectiveness**

In spite of the need for comprehensiveness, impact assessment documents can become unnecessarily bulky if undue attention is paid to and undeserved effort dissipated on trivialities. Thus, while not completely discountenancing negligible and/or insignificant issues, a good impact assessment method must be able to focus attention on major factors. In this regard, such a method must be designed to be able to eliminate, as early as possible, un-important impacts, by providing a basis for determining the potential significance of an impact, even at the early stages of assessment.

**Exclusiveness**

It is very easy to double-count, or duplicates impacts, For instance, loss of vegetation would necessarily imply loss of wildlife habitat. Thus, while this may not necessarily mean destruction of wildlife (since they can migrate), double-counting could occur, if loss of vegetation is regarded as a separate impact from destruction of wildlife habitat. To this end therefore, a sound assessment method must make concerted efforts to avoid such occurrences, even though expedience has shown that this is difficult because of the many interrelationships that exist in a natural environment.

**Confidence**

The level of confidence about the possibility of an impact occurring or not occurring is important in the overall rating of the significance of an impact. Therefore, in assessment, a sound method must have provision for indicating confidence levels for each impact predicted. Therefore, adequate information must be provided on assumptions made, so that they are open to critical examination, and if necessary, alterations to suit realities on ground.

**Objectiveness**

A sound assessment method must exclude bias, as much as possible. For instance, a Muslim would regard the removal of wild pig species from an environment as a positive impact, based on religious consideration. However, this may not necessarily be true from an ecological viewpoint. Therefore, provisions must be made in any method, to remove subjectivity, by including objectiveness. Several agencies, including the Lagos State Ministry of the Environment and Water Resources and the Federal Ministry of Environment (FMEnv) have emphasized this. Objectivity minimizes the possibility that the predictions automatically support the preconceived notions of the promoter and/or assessor. These prejudgments are usually caused by a lack of knowledge of local conditions or insensitivity to public opinion.

A second reason for objectivity is to ensure comparability of EIA predictions amongst similar types of actions. Several methods are generally used for impact prediction and analyses. Some of the more popular and internationally accepted options include the following:
*   Checklists
*   Matrices
*   Flowcharts and Networks
*   Mathematical/Statistical models
*   Overlays using maps and GIS

It is very obvious that no single method can have all of the attributes described above, thus, in order to optimize on impact assessment, different groups have over the years evolved methods that have the positive aspects of some or all of the options listed above. For this proposed project, a method was evolved that incorporated all of the foregoing. The methodology is summarized in Figure 5.1, while a description of the process and the results obtained from applying the method is described in the following sub-sections.

**Figure 5.1: Methodological Process for Impact Assessment**

## Methodological Process for Impact Assessment

1. **Step 1: Identification of Project Activities**
   
2. **Step 2: Preliminary identification of potential impacts on biophysical, social and health components of the environment.**
   
3. **Step 3: Screening of Impacts**
   
4. **Step 4: Detailed assessment of selected focus impacts under the following bases:**
   - Nature: Positive or Negative; direct or indirect
   - Magnitude: Qualitative and Quantitative
   - Extent: Qualitative and Quantitative
   - Timing and Duration: Temporary, permanent, short-term, long-term
   - Reversibility: Reversible or irreversible
   - Likelihood (risk or probability) of occurrence
   
5. **Step 5: Identification of Mitigation Measures**

**5.2 Preliminary Identification and Screening of Environmental Impacts**

In line with widely recommended impact assessment, approaches (FMEnv. 1995; UNEP, 1996; Canter, 1996; DPR 2002, Lohani et al., 1997) the first level of impact assessment involves the preliminary identification and screening of potential environmental impacts from anticipated activity-environment interactions based on an understanding of the activities and the nature of interaction with environmental components. A modified Leopold matrix (Leopold, 1971) is then used for the identification and screening, The matrix arrays project activities against environmental (biophysical, socio-economic and health) components, and supports a methodical, comprehensive, and objective identification of the impacts each project activity may have on each biophysical, socioeconomic and health component.

Impact identification is based on Wathern (1988), who defines an impact as "having both spatial and temporal components and can be described as the change in an environmental parameter over a specified period within a defined area, resulting from a particular activity compared with the situation which would have occurred had the activity not been initiated". To further guide the identification and screening of impacts using the matrix, established environmental impact indicators or indices are developed, for each of the environmental interaction categories. Impact indicators are the observable or measurable parameters of each environmental component that can be directly or indirectly linked to changes in environmental conditions. Table 5.1 gives the project phases and the summary of related activities. Table 5.2 gives the specific environmental components and sub-elements to be used as indicators while Table 5.3 presents a description of the indicators.

**Table 5.1 Project Phases and Associated Activities**

| PHASES | ACTIVITIES |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Pre-Construction** | Mobilization of equipment and men to site |
| | Site Clearing activities |
| **Construction Phase** | Mobilization of the equipment/ machineries, materials and men for construction activities; |
| | Construction of Camp and Ancillary Facilities |
| | Full Site clearing activities |
| | Actual construction of the building and ancillary building |

| **Decommissioning/Abandonment Phase**| Demolition of Structures |

| | Management of Demolition Wastes |

**Table 5.3: Environmental Components and their Impact Indicators**

| Environmental Components | Impact Indicators |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Biophysical** | |
| Climate | Temperature, Rainfall, Relative Humidity, Windspeed and direction. |
| Vegetation | Changes in vegetation abundance and species composition as well as biomass productivity |
| Groundwater Quality | Changes to basic water quality indices such as pH, conductivity, heavy metals and total hydrocarbons |
| Air Quality and noise levels | Changes in background values of basic air quality indices such as TSP, hydrocarbons, NOx, SOx, Co, etc. Increase in background ambient noise levels |

| Conflicts | Communal strife between project workers and neighbouring communities |

The modified Leopold impact matrix consists of a horizontal list of biophysical, socioeconomic and health environmental components that could be affected by the proposed project activities versus a vertical list of project activities, which represent environmental aspects, or "sources of impact," associated with each project phase. Environmental aspects are elements of an activity that can or will interact with the biophysical, socio economic and health conditions within the area of influence. Entries in the matrix cells represent the nature and preliminary ranking of the severity of the impact. Ranking of the severity is based on the following scale and symbols:
*   Major - (2)
*   Minor - (1)
*   Negligible and/or no effect - (-) (i.e., a dash).
*   Positive (+)

For this preliminary impact assessment stage, the impacts are defined as:
*   **A Major impact** is one that would affect a large (higher than 40%) amount of a resource and or have a relatively large footprint and persist for a long time or is irreversible.
*   **A Minor impact** is one that could either affect a large (as defined above) or moderate (less than 40%) amount of an affected resource, has a mid to long-term effect but is most likely reversible.
*   **A Negligible impact** is one that may occur but based on experience, available scientific information and expert knowledge will have no measurable effect on the environmental component.
*   **A Positive impact** is one that adds a measurable benefit to the environment

All number entries denote negative impacts. Cells with Positive sign (+) and numbers) indicate a positive and negative impact for the specific activity- environment interaction. All potential impacts, whether likely or unlikely, are also considered at this stage. The 'likelihood of an impact is further assessed in the detailed impact evaluation. Identification and screening of impacts relied on the following:
*   Documented impacts of similar projects in similar environments
*   Consultation with experts
*   Professional judgment.
*   Results of earlier environmental studies carried out in the area
*   Spatial boundaries of interaction were decided based on specialist knowledge and documented experience of the specific activity-environment interaction.

**5.3 Detailed Assessment of Impacts (STEP 4)**

The preliminary identification and screening of environmental impacts resulted in a group of focus impacts (those with impact rankings of 1 and 2), which were further assessed in terms of severity and significance. Impact severity and significance criteria used at the next stage relied on a number of resources and tools including the following:
*   Department of Petroleum Resources (DPR) and Federal Ministry of Environment, (FMEnv) EIA Guidelines
*   Overlaying project components on maps of existing conditions to identify potential impact areas and issues
*   Environmental Baseline Studies conducted specifically for this project
*   Consultation with Nigerian experts and residents
*   Results of earlier studies carried out on the project.
*   Experience from similar projects in Nigeria and worldwide
*   Published and unpublished documents (such as The World Bank Environmental Assessment Sourcebook and other authoritative texts on performing environmental impact assessments) providing guidance on performing impact analysis for industrial development activities
*   UNEP EIA Training Resources Manual (1996).
*   European Commission Guidance on EIA EIS Review (European Commission, 2001)

The approach applied to this proposed Steel Pipe Production project EIA also incorporates the following key elements:

**Impact Severity Evaluation**

A number of criteria are used to assess the severity of the environmental (biophysical, socio economic and health) impacts that were not screened out in the earlier steps. The severity criteria set forth in this section are widely applicable to all types of impacts identified, including impacts that can be expected from the project and impacts resulting from emergencies. Several types of potential consequences (or impacts) were considered for all project stages where applicable:
1.  Natural (physical, chemical and biological) environment
2.  Socio-economic environment
3.  Health and Safety of the public or workers

The detailed assessment of impacts also involved evaluating the potential effects of project activities on the same impact indicators earlier defined but at a greater detail, Impacts were assessed as to whether they are positive (beneficial) or negative (detrimental). Five impact severity evaluation criteria were applied to this study; Magnitude, Duration, Frequency, Areal Extent, and Sensitivity of the Receptor, Within these five criteria, impacts were also evaluated with respect to whether they will result in cumulative effects, incremental changes, or indirect (secondary) effects. The overall impact evaluation considers not only the potential severity of the impact but also the likelihood of its occurrence.

**Magnitude** is defined as the quantitative intensity of the impact, and can be measured as the percentage of a resource or a population within the area of influence, that may be affected by an impact. The definitions of "high," "medium" and "low" with respect to Magnitude may vary depending upon the specific receptor. The Magnitude of an impact may be characterized as follows:
*   **High** - large amount of the resource or population is affected; an easily observable and measurable effect
*   **Medium** - moderate amount of the resource or population is affected; generally measurable and observable effect
*   **Low** - small amount of the resource or population is affected; a low magnitude impact may be within the range of normal variation of background conditions
*   **Negligible** - the amount of resource or population affected is unnoticeable or immeasurably small

Magnitude may also be defined with respect to quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria, if available and applicable, (e.g., level of noise impact in units of decibels). The Magnitude of an impact may be characterized as follows:
*   **High** - greater than the quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria
*   **Medium** - at the quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria
*   **Low** - less than the quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria
*   **Negligible** - impact not detected or at background conditions

**Duration** is defined as the time that is estimated for a population or resource to return to conditions present prior to the impact. The duration is calculated from the time the impact begins or which may coincide with the start of the activity that causes the impact. The Duration of an impact may be characterized as follows:
*   **High** -long-term impact (recovery would not occur within ten years)
*   **Medium** -moderate-term impact (recovery time between one year and ten years)
*   **Low** -short-term impact (recovery time within less than one year)
*   **Negligible** - impact or recovery is very short term or immediate

Characterization of the Duration of an impact as low, medium, or high includes consideration of the Degree of Reversibility of the impact. Impacts for which the Duration is classified as high, as defined above, would be irreversible impacts.

**Frequency** is defined as the number of times an impact is expected to occur over the life of the project. The Frequency of an impact may be characterized as follows:
*   **High** - continuous impact; Impact will occur continuously throughout the life of the project (e.g., continuous process wastewater discharge)
*   **Medium** - intermittent impact: Impact will occur intermittently over the life of the project (e.g., dredging for sand, selling the dredged sand, etc.)
*   **Low** - rarely occurring impact: Impact will occur a very limited number of times (e.g., construction impacts)

There is no "negligible" category for frequency because impacts with no frequency would not occur, and were screened out.

**Areal Extent** refers to the potential areal extent of an impact, and may be quantified in units of area affected (e.g., square kilometres). The Areal Extent of an impact may be characterized as follows:
*   **High** - impact to the national, regional, or global environment (e.g., greenhouse gas emissions)
*   **Medium** - impact to the general vicinity of the project site or study area
*   **Low** - impact limited to the immediate vicinity of the activity or occurrence that results in the impact
*   **Negligible** - impact limited to a very small part of the activity area

**Sensitivity of the Receptor** refers to economic, social, and/or environmental/ecological importance of the receptor, including the receptors' intrinsic sensitivity, reliance on the receptor by people for sustenance, livelihood, or economic activity, and to the importance of direct impacts to persons associated with the resource. Impacts that directly affect people or vital natural resources are deemed to be more important than impacts that indirectly affect people or vital resources. The Sensitivity of the receptor criterion also refers to potential impacts to Environmentally Sensitive Areas (ESAs) and impacts to species, including loss of endangered species, effects of introduction of invasive species, and similar environmental/ecological impacts. The intrinsic sensitivities of a receptor species and actions that alter the function of the receptor are also considered. Sensitivity of the Receptor may be characterized as follows:
*   **High** - receptor is of high economic, social, and/or environmental importance and or has an intrinsic sensitivity (including vulnerability and exposure) to the specific impact (e.g., fresh water resources and mangroves).
*   **Medium** - receptor is of moderate economic, social, and/or environmental importance and is not particularly vulnerable and/or exposed to the impact.
*   **Low** - receptor is of low economic, social, and/or environmental importance and is not vulnerable and/or exposed to the specific impact.
*   **Negligible** - receptor is not of economic, social, and/or environmental importance or is not sensitive to impact.

These significance criteria are applied to each of the potential impacts initially identified during the screening process to determine whether they would likely be negligible, minor, moderate, or major. The impact assessment at this stage takes into consideration design mitigation measures. Those issues determined to be inconsequential or not applicable after consideration of the design mitigation measures are eliminated from or "screened out" from further consideration.

To reach an overall impact severity rating for each impact assessed, the five impacts severity criteria mentioned above are further aggregated using impact severity matrices. Aggregation is at three levels. First, Impact Magnitude and Areal Extent are combined to arrive at a rating for the Impact Quantum (Impact Quantum is a function of the magnitude and areal extent as earlier defined), while Duration and Frequency are aggregated to give the overall Temporal Effects. Impact Quantum and Temporal Effects are then combined and their resulting aggregate assessed in terms of sensitivity to arrive at the overall impact severity. Figures 5-2 to 5-5 show the aggregation process.

A qualitative and where possible, quantitative discussion of the potential for cumulative effects is then used to further qualify the impact based on knowledge of other attendant or anticipated stress factors.

**Figure 5.2: Impact Severity Matrix for Impact Quantum**

| Magnitude \ Areal Extent | Negligible | Low | Medium | High |
|--------------------------|------------|-----|--------|------|
| High                     | Medium     | Medium | High | High |
| Medium                   | Low        | Medium | Medium | High |
| Low                      | Negligible | Low | Medium | Medium |
| Negligible               | Negligible | Negligible | Low | Low |

**Figure 5.3: Impact Severity Matrix for Temporal Effect**

| Frequency \ Duration | Negligible | Low | Medium | High |
|----------------------|------------|-----|--------|------|
| High                 | Medium     | Medium | High | High |
| Medium               | Low        | Medium | Medium | High |
| Low                  | Negligible | Low | Medium | Medium |
| Negligible           | Negligible | Negligible | Low | Low |

**Figure 5.4: Impact Severity Matrix for Quantum and Temporal Effects**

| Temporal Effects \ Impact Quantum | High | Medium | Low | Negligible |
|-----------------------------------|------|--------|-----|------------|
| High                              | Major | Major | Moderate | Minor |
| Medium                            | Major | Moderate | Moderate | Minor |
| Low                               | Moderate | Minor | Minor | Negligible |
| Negligible                        | Minor | Minor | Negligible | Negligible |

**Figure 5.5: Overall Impact Severity Rating Matrix**

| Impact Quantum & Temporal Effects \ Sensitivity of Receptor | High | Medium | Low | Negligible |
|-------------------------------------------------------------|------|--------|-----|------------|
| Major                                                       | Major | Major | Moderate | Minor |
| Moderate                                                    | Major | Moderate | Moderate | Minor |
| Minor                                                       | Moderate | Minor | Minor | Negligible |
| Negligible                                                  | Minor | Minor | Negligible | Negligible |

**Impact Likelihood Evaluation (STEP 5)**

To further assess the significance of the severity associated with each potential negative impact identified in the previous section, likelihood criteria are applied to each negative impact (Table 5.4). The likelihood criteria are used to determine whether negative impacts can be prevented, mitigated, or is unavoidable. It should be noted that the likelihood criteria is applied to the likelihood of the impact occurring and not the activity occurring, for example, the sinking of the dredge vessel. The overall severity rating (significance) of a negative environmental impact is a function of its severity as earlier defined and the likelihood of occurrence as defined in Table 5-4. For example, a moderate impact that has a high likelihood of occurrence would be more severe than a major impact with a very low likelihood of occurrence. Assigning a significance ranking and a likelihood ranking to each impact allows for semi-quantitative evaluation of the severity of the impact.

**Table 5.4: Impact Likelihood Criteria**

| Likelihood Level | Definition |
| :--- | :--- |
| **Very Low** | Impact has approximately less than 1 or 2 percent likelihood of occurring; impact unknown to have previously resulted in similar circumstances in the industry. |
| **Low** | Impact highly unlikely, given the controls in place (e.g., between approximately 2 to 20 percent likelihood of occurring, impact has been known to result, but only very rarely, in similar circumstances). |
| **Medium** | Impact could occur infrequently during normal operations, but given a breakdown of the safeguards and controls (i.e. lack of maintenance for a protecting device) it could occur more readily (e.g., between approximately 20 to 70 percent likelihood of occurring, impact has been known to result in many similar circumstances, but does not result routinely) |
| **High** | Given the controls in place, the impact is likely to occur during normal operations (e.g., over 70 percent likelihood of occurring, impact has been known to result routinely, though not necessarily in all similar circumstances). |

**Table 5.5: Summary of Impact Severity**

| | Magnitude | Duration | Frequency | Areal Extent | Sensitivity of Receptor |
| :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **High** | Large amount of resource or population affected; easily measurable OR > than the quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria | Long-term impact (recovery would not occur within ten years) | Continuous impact: impact will occur continuously throughout the life of the project (e.g., continuous process emissions from power generating sets and vehicles) | Impact to the national, regional, or global environment (e.g., greenhouse gas emissions) | Receptor is of high economic, social, and/or environmental importance. Has very high intrinsic sensitivity, e.g., sensitivity of juveniles to spills. |
| **Moderate**| Moderate amount of resource or population affected; generally measurable, observable OR At the quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria | Moderate-term impact (recovery time between one year and ten years) | Intermittent impact: impact will occur intermittently over the life of the project (e.g., noise emissions from vehicles). | Impact to the general vicinity of the project site or study area | Receptor is of moderate economic, social, and/or environmental importance; has a moderate intrinsic sensitivity. |
| **Minor** | Small amount of resource or population affected; low magnitude impact may be within range of normal OR Less than the quantitative or semi-quantitative criteria | Short-term impact (recovery time within one year) | Rarely occurring impact: Impact will occur a very limited number of times (e.g., construction impacts) | Impact limited to the immediate vicinity of the activity or occurrence that results in the impact | Receptor is of low economic, social, and/or environmental importance; has low intrinsic sensitivity. |
| **Negligible**| Amount of resource or population affected is unnoticeable or immeasurably small OR Impact not detected or at background conditions | Impact or recovery is very short term or immediate | Never occurring impact: occurrence of impact is almost impossible | Impact limited to a very small part of the activity area | Receptor is not of economic, social, and/or environmental importance or is not sensitive to impact |

The colour coded impact severity matrix presented in Figure 5.6 illustrates the application of the impact severity and likelihood. The likelihood ranking is placed in the y-axis and the impact significance ranking in the x-axis. The colour codes are also used in the text discussing each impact assessed using this method.

**Figure 5.6: Impact Significance Matrix**
| Likelihood \ Impact Severity | Beneficial | Low Significance | Moderate Significance | High Significance |
|------------------------------|------------|------------------|-----------------------|-------------------|
| High                         | Yellow     | Red              | Red                   | Red               |
| Medium                       | Green      | Yellow           | Red                   | Red               |
| Low                          | Green      | Green            | Yellow                | Yellow            |
| Very Low                     | Green      | Green            | Green                 | Yellow            |

The overall impact significance level is indicated by the position on the impact significance matrix. For example, impacts placed within the red boxes have a high likelihood of occurrence and serious consequence; thus they have a high significance rating. These high-significance impacts become high priority issues for further evaluation or management action. Similarly, impacts in the yellow category are moderate impacts, with a medium priority. Impacts in the green boxes are low and are given lowest priority, Impacts identified by the white boxes indicate positive or beneficial impacts. The criteria and severity matrix set forth in this section is widely applicable to all the types of events and impacts identified.

**5.4 IMPACT ANALYSIS**

This section of the report analyses the associated and potential impacts of activities of the various phases of the project.

**5.4.1 Potential Positive Impacts of the Proposed Project**

There are some positive impacts likely to arise from the proposed project. The basic and most critical positive impacts include the following:

**Creation of Employment Opportunities:**
The proposed project will provide temporary and some permanent employment opportunities. Direct employment shall be created through the engagement of skilled and unskilled labour during the construction phase of the project thereby empowering people financially and reducing the tendency for engaging in social vices, Some indirect employment opportunities shall be created through supply of construction materials and provision of sundry services. Also, some permanent jobs will be created for facility maintenance, provision security amongst others. The proposed construction and operation of the planned development will create socio-economic interaction within the project area.

**Stimulation of Economic Growth**
The injection of the project cost into the local economy will help in stimulating economic activities around the project corridor. The planned project will surely create employment opportunities and this will lead to other business; opportunities within the project area thereby improving

**Reduction in Crime and Social Vices**
The proposed project through its employment creation potentials will contribute to the reduction in crime and social vices as some of the idle youths that would have hitherto been involved in criminal activities would have been gainfully employed.

**Increase in Revenue to Government**
The construction and operation of the proposed development will result in generation of revenue for government through payment of statutory Levies and Taxes.

**5.4.2 Potential Negative Impacts**

**Mobilization Phase Impacts**

This is the planning phase of the project when there will be movement of goods, personnel (workers) and equipment machineries to the project site. Given the magnitude of the project, large numbers of personnel and materials will need to be mobilized and as such, a number of impacts are expected to result from this activity. Some of these impacts will include:

**Impact on Noise Level**
The movement of equipment, machineries and workers to site will lead to minimal vehicular traffic that will result increase noise within the project area as a result of noise generated from vehicles and machineries. The magnitude of this impact is considered to be low given the fact that the mobilization of equipment and workers will happen within limited period and will be restricted to the route to the project area. In terms of frequency, the impact will occur intermittently during the construction phase. Impact duration is therefore low as it will be short lived each time it occurs. The sensitivity of the resources to noise impacts is considered low and the impact is reversible. The likelihood of the impact occurring is moderate since the movement of equipment, machineries and workers are certain to occur. The overall severity rating of the impact is low. The impact significance is therefore of overall low significance.

**Impact on Ambient Air quality**
The movement of equipment, machineries and workers to site will lead to minimal vehicular traffic that will result in emission from vehicle conveying workers and from machineries being mobilized to site thereby impacting on the ambient air quality. The magnitude of this impact is considered to be low given the fact that the movement will be restricted to the vicinity of the project area. The areal extent of the impact is low when compared to the entire size of the free zone, In terms of frequency, the impact will occur intermittently during the preconstruction activities. Impact duration is therefore low as it will be short lived each time it occurs. The sensitivity of the resources to impact is considered medium and the impact is reversible. The likelihood of the impact occurring is moderate since the movement of equipment, machineries and workers are certain to occur. The overall severity rating of the impact is low. The impact significance is therefore of overall low significance.

**Impact on Traffic**
The mobilization of materials, machineries and workers to site would be done by road and this could result in increase in vehicular traffic along the along Lagos-Badagry Expressway corridor. The magnitude of the impact will be moderate given the fact that the movement shall be planned for off-peak periods to reduce the possibility of causing traffic jams. The areal extent of the impact is medium considering the fact the movement activities extend outside the project environment. This impact would be short term and with the implementation of an efficient Traffic and Journey Management Plan, the duration of impact will be low as the mobilization to site would only occur for few days. The likelihood of the impact occurring is moderate since the movement of equipment, machineries and workers are certain to occur. The overall severity rating of the impact is medium as the mobilization will be planned for off-peak period. The impact significance is therefore of overall moderate significance.

**Impact on Existing infrastructure**
The movement of materials and personnel to the project site by road will no doubt put additional pressure on the existing road infrastructure. The magnitude of the impact will be low given the fact that the movement shall be planned for off-peak periods to reduce the possibility of causing stress on other road users. The areal extent of the impact is medium considering the fact the movement activities extend outside the project environment. This impact would be short term and with the implementation of an efficient Traffic and Journey Management Plan, the duration of impact will be low as the mobilization to site would only occur for few days. The likelihood of the impact occurring is moderate since the movement of equipment, machineries and workers are certain to occur. The overall severity rating of the impact is low since the mobilization will be planned for off-peak period and would be short-term. The impact significance is therefore of overall low significance.

**Impact on Public Health and Safety**
The movement of heavy trucks and equipment/ machineries could increase the risk of accidents/injuries due to increase in road traffic and exposure to noise increase that could affect the public health and safety. The possibility of occurrence is low as all project drivers would be made to pass through safe driving training before commencement of project.The likelihood of the impact occurring is moderate since the movement of equipment, machineries and workers are certain to occur. The overall severity rating of the impact is low since the mobilization will be planned for off-peak period and would be short-term. The impact significance is therefore of overall low significance.

**Site Preparation Phase Impacts**

**Impacts on Air Quality (Impairment of Air Quality)**
Air-borne particulates would result from disturbances to the soil during construction and site preparation activities. A lot of dust would be generated during pilling. All diesel-powered facilities such as electricity generators and heavy duty equipment as well as vehicles would emit SO2, CO2, N0X and other gases. Degradation of air quality could occur due to emissions from vehicles. The emissions are short-termed and expected to be localized within the immediate project environment. Though the likelihood of occurrence is high, the consequence is rated a negligible negative. Thus, the overall impact risk level is expected to be minor. The duration of the impact will be moderate as construction will be a short while. The frequency of the impact will be moderate, as the impact will occur intermittently throughout the construction period.

**Impact on Noise Level**
During site preparation a lot of noise will be generated particularly during foundations pilling works, iron cutting and welding works as well as vehicular movement. Noise levels arising from these activities though expected to exceed ambient levels at times will be transient and localized. Given the fact that noise levels are not expected to significantly exceed the existing background, the sensitivity of the receptor is classified minor and overall risk level is expected to be low, since impact is expected to be temporary.

**Impacts on Soil**
The potential impacts on soil resources are closely related to site clearing, site preparation and construction of site camp. These could manifest mostly as soil erosion, land degradation and fugitive dust released into atmosphere. Other significant potential effects on the soil include compaction, changes in drainage patterns and contamination from discharges, leakages and accidental releases. It is also expected that grading and compaction of soil would lead to loss of organic matter, alteration of soil structure and reduction in filtration, water holding capacity, aeration and root penetration. Alteration to soil conditions can cause widespread secondary impacts by reducing the capacity of the habitat to support flora and fauna. Also, sand filling of the site with soil materials from other sources could result in the transfer of soil contaminants from point of purchase to the project site

**Impacts on Groundwater**
Site Preparation is not expected to disturb the flow of groundwater in the area, as only the topmost layer of the earth materials would be involved during site preparation. The only possibility of impact on the groundwater is expected to occur in the remote case of percolation of materials, oils and grease and wastes if not properly stored. This possibility is remote considering the site management plan that will be put in place. Therefore, the impact is considered negligible negative with low likelihood. The overall risk rating is low.

*   **Loss of Biodiversity**
    Site preparation activities will involve the clearing of the vegetation on the project site and sand filling. These activities will without any doubts lead to loss of flora and fauna that are native to the project area. Site preparation will obviously result in massive loss of biodiversity within the project area. The likelihood of impact occurrence is high and impact significance is also high as loss of biodiversity is irreversible and permanent

*   **Loss of Natural Habitats**
    The site preparation activities at the project site will result in the loss of natural habitat for some fauna and flora that are native to the project environment. The implication of this is that some of the native fauna will migrate to other safer environment while some endangered species may go into extinction from the area. The migration of some species from the project area to other areas may result in species competing for habitats. This impact is irreversible and permanent. The likelihood of occurrence is high and impact significance is rated high

**Impacts on Traffic and Transportation**
In the course of site preparation activities, there will be need to transport materials and men to the project site at various times. The increased presence of trucks associated with the site preparation activities may further worsen the sometime difficult traffic situation in the area

**Impacts on Waste Management**
A lot of wastes are expected to be generated during the site preparation phase of this project. These would include wood cuttings from cleared vegetation, pet bottles, packaging material, tins, welding electrodes, etc. Human wastes generated from the construction workers could constitute aesthetic issues for the project area. Wastes if allowed to accumulate could lead to contamination of soil and groundwater as well as the existing water body, particularly if percolation and run off into the waters is allowed. All wastes arising from construction activities will be evacuated from the site for proper disposal by the Lagos State Waste Management Authority (LAWMA) or its appointed contractor

**Impacts on Public Health and Safety**
The site preparation phase of the project would definitely bring about the movement of different people including skilled and unskilled labour force and service providers. This has its own attendant health and safety implications. The health and safety problems that could be associated with the project could be classified as:
(a) **Communicable diseases** - Skin infections, sexually transmitted diseases, dysentery, respiratory tract infections etc
(b) **Non-communicable diseases** - include those as a result of inhalation of fumes from vehicles, machineries which could result in health problems. Allergic reaction may also arise from the fumes.
(c) **Injuries** - There may be injury and even accident

**Construction Phase Impacts**

This section of the report analyses the associated and potential impacts of construction activities related to the project.

*   **Impacts on Air Quality**
    Air-borne particulates would result from disturbances to the soil during construction activities of the proposed project. For instance, a lot of dust would be generated during pilling. All diesel-powered facilities such as electricity generators and heavy-duty equipment as well as vehicles would emit SO2, CO2, N0X and other gases. Degradation of air quality could occur due to emissions from vehicles. The emissions are short-termed and localized within the immediate project environment. Though the likelihood of occurrence is high, the consequence is rated a negligible negative. Thus, the overall impact risk level is expected to be minor. The duration of the impact will be moderate as construction activities are expected to continue for not less than six (6) months. The frequency of the impact will be moderate, as the impact will occur intermittently throughout the construction period.

*   **Impact on Noise Level**
    During construction, a lot of noise will be generated particularly during foundations, pilling, iron cutting and welding works as well as vehicular movement. Noise levels arising from these activities though expected to exceed ambient levels at times will be transient and localized. Given the fact that noise levels are not expected to significantly exceed the existing background and the fact that the area is already quite used to high levels of noise from vehicular movements, the sensitivity of the receptor is classified minor and overall risk level is expected to be low, since impact is expected to be temporary.

*   **Impacts on Geology (Alteration to Site Geology)**
    The study area lies in a very geological (both tectonic and seismic) stable region with no recorded cases of earthquakes or tremors. In addition, no major or minor geological hazards are known to occur in the area. Only minimal geological impacts are expected in the construction phase of the project which is related basically to the exaction of top soil for construction works. No topographic or geologic alteration due to the construction of the proposed development is expected. Though the site requires sand filling, the sand filling activities are not expected to cause any form of geological alterations Soil erosion is not anticipated as the adequate control measures will be put in place. Impact consequence from construction activities is rated a negligible negative, while the likelihood of its occurrence is low, thus the overall risk is low.

*   **Impacts on Soil**
    The potential impacts on soil resources are closely related to site clearing, site preparation and construction. These could manifest mostly as soil erosion, land degradation and fugitive dust released into atmosphere. Other significant potential effects on the soil include compaction, changes in drainage patterns and contamination from discharges, leakages and accidental releases. It is also expected that grading and compaction of soil would lead to loss of organic matter, alteration of soil structure and reduction in filtration, water holding capacity, aeration and root penetration. Alteration to soil conditions can cause widespread secondary impacts by reducing the capacity of the habitat to support flora and fauna. The impact level is negatively moderate as its consequences are localized within the project area. The likelihood of occurrence is high however; in view of the temporary nature of the construction work, overall impact risk is considered low.

*   **Impacts on Groundwater**
    There is potentials for percolation of materials such as oils, used lubricants and wastes if not properly stored. This possibility is remote considering the site management plan that will be put in place. Therefore, the impact is considered negligible negative with low likelihood. The overall risk rating is low.

*   **Impacts on Waste Management**
    A lot of wastes would be generated during the construction phase of the project. These would include metal cuttings, packaging material, anti-corrosion chemicals and paints, empty drums and tins, welding electrodes, etc. Human wastes generated from the construction workers could constitute aesthetic issues for the project area. Wastes if allowed to accumulate could lead to contamination of soil and groundwater, particularly if percolation and run off into the waters is allowed. All wastes arising from construction activities will be evacuated from the site, for proper disposal by the Lagos State Waste Management Authority (LAWMA) or its appointed contractor.

**Construction Phase Impacts (Socio Economics)**

In addition to the environmental impacts described above, the construction of this proposed project would impact on the local socio-economic framework in a number of ways.

**Impacts on Land-Use and Availability**
The proposed project site is zoned residential and there already exist within the area residential developments. The sitting of the proposed project in the area would only enhance the compatibility of the land use with the existing land uses in the area. However, once the proposed project is constructed on the site, the option for converting the site to other land uses would be highly limited. Also, the proposed project site will also no longer be available for use.

**Impacts on Traffic and Transportation**
In the course of constructing the proposed Structure, there will be need to transport materials and men to the project site at various times. In addition other project components such as foundation equipment will also be transported to site. The increased presence of heavy-duty trucks associated with the construction activities may further worsen the already difficult traffic situation in the area and could increase the potentials for accidents. This could lead to physiological stress on the people in the area.

**Impacts on Public Health and Safety**
The construction phase of the project would definitely bring about the movement of different people including skilled and unskilled labour force and service providers. This has its own attendant health and safety problems. The health and safety problems that could be associated with the project could be classified as:
(a) **Communicable diseases** - Skin infections, sexually transmitted diseases, dysentery, respiratory tract infections etc.
(b) **Non-communicable diseases** - include those as a result of inhalation of fumes from vehicles, machineries that could result in health problems. Allergic reaction may also arise from the fumes.
The increased presence of heavy-duty trucks associated with the construction activities may create difficult traffic situation in the area and could increase the potentials for accidents. Since the project site is located along a major highway, there is the potentials for workers or visitors to the site to be hit by vehicles plying the highway

**Impact on Historical and Cultural Resources**
No cultural heritage resources were found within and around the project site, There will be no impacts to cultural resources on archaeological materials as none was found within the project area

**Operation/ Maintenance Phase Impacts**

*   **Impacts on Air Quality and Climate**
    During operation, direct and negative impacts could result from generating sets, vehicles travelling to and from the project site. In this regard, the impact of operations of the terminal facility on air quality is rated as minor risk, with a minor negative consequence and low likelihood of occurrence.

*   **Impacts on Noise Level**
    The noise that shall be generated from the operation of the proposed Container Terminal development is not expected to be above the recommended 70 decibels by NESREA for commercial area as there would hardly be any activities that could generate such level of noise. It would be safe therefore to conclude that impacts due to noise levels shall be low with a low likelihood of occurrence and low risk impact.

*   **Impacts on Soil**
    Potential impacts to soil during the operational phase could occur through the improper use, storage and handling of the materials such as petroleum products and solid wastes generated on site. The comprehensive environmental procedures prepared for the project will ensure that any potential impacts are adequately mitigated. Thus impact level is minor negative consequence, with a low likelihood of occurrence and overall risk level adjudged low.

*   **Impacts on Groundwater**
    During operational phase groundwater resources could be negatively impacted through leakage of petroleum product storage facilities on site or accidental spills. The management plan that shall be put in place will make spills and accidental discharges a very rare case. Also the seepage of sewage/ wastewater into the ground could impact negatively on the ground water in the project area. Adequate provision has been made to ensure all liquid wastes either sewage or waste water are well treated before discharge into the environment. Therefore the overall impact rating of the impact is seen as low with low likelihood of occurrence and medium negative impact.

**Impacts on Socio-Economics**

*   **Impacts on Transportation**
    The transportation impacts resulting from the operation of the proposed development will be in terms of increased in vehicular traffic as a result of residents and visitors to the facility. The magnitude of this impact will be moderate. Although the project area is small, the traffic-build up would definitely extend well beyond the immediate environment of the project. The duration and frequency of impact will both be major as the impact will occur continuously throughout the lifetime of the project. The truth is that the project area is already subject to substantial vehicular traffic, the add-on effect on traffic will be minimal, even though the effect on the population cannot be ignored. In this regard the severity of the impact in terms of the sensitivity of the receptor is rated moderate.

*   **Fire Hazards**
    Fires may result either by operational omissions or commission and/or through unanticipated lightening discharges and/ or sometimes from high voltages from electricity distribution company This event if allowed to occur, could lead to loss of lives and property at the project site and the fire may spread to adjourning facilities, causing unquantifiable damage, The proponent already has a standing arrangement with both the state and federal fire services as well as a robust Emergency Response Plan. However, there shall be provision of comprehensive fire prevention and fire- fighting equipment for the structure. In addition, all residents shall be taken through appropriate Emergency Response and Evacuation trainings and drills periodically

*   **Impact on Security Arrangement of the Project Area**
    The existence of the proposed development in the project area could bring about new security challenges as more people and businesses will be attracted to the project area. This may result in increase in crimes and social vices in the area and will obviously impact on the existing security arrangement in the project area and stretch the host community security infrastructure

*   **Impact on Existing Infrastructure/Amenities**
    The existence of the proposed development in the project area could put additional pressure on the existing infrastructure/ utilities in the area such as roads, hospital, schools, shopping malls, recreational facilities, waste management facility amongst others. For instance, the Connection of the facility to the national grid for electricity supply will increase electricity consumption in the project area. Also, there may be movement of more people into the area thus increasing the number of vehicles plying the Lagos-Badagry Expressway, thus putting addition pressure on the road.

**Cumulative Impacts**

Cumulative impact means the impact on the environment which results from the incremental impact of the action when added to other past, present, and reasonably foreseeable future actions regardless of what agency or person undertakes such other actions. Cumulative impacts can result from individually minor but collectively significant actions taking place over a period of time.

For the proposed development, the cumulative impacts include:
*   **Traffic Congestion**
    The construction and operation phases of the proposed development will without any doubts add on to the existing traffic situation around mowo junction and the immediate environment. This impact is significant and will require coordinated effort of all stakeholders within the corridor

**Residual Impacts**

Residual impacts are changes resulting from the implementation of the proposed project that remain or can be observed even after the implementation of mitigation measures. These impacts exist for as long as the project exists. For the proposed project, the residual impacts are discussed below:
*   **Impact of Landtake**
    The proposed project involves the use of the available land space on the project site. The implication of this is that for as long as the project exist, the land taken for the project will no longer be available for other uses

*   **Change in the Aesthetics and Landscape**
    With the emergence of the proposed development, there will be change in the aesthetics and landscape of the project area. This impact is expected to continue as long as the project exist
